   <h1 class="firstHeading" id="firstHeading" lang="en">
    List of
    <i>
     South Park
    </i>
    characters
   </h1>
   <div class="mw-body-content" id="bodyContent">
    <div id="siteSub">
     From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia
    </div>
    <div id="contentSub">
     <span class="mw-redirectedfrom">
      (Redirected from
      <a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_characters_in_South_Park&amp;redirect=no" title="List of characters in South Park">
       List of characters in South Park
      </a>
      )
     </span>
    </div>
    <div class="mw-jump" id="jump-to-nav">
     Jump to:
     <a href="#mw-head">
      navigation
     </a>
     ,
     <a href="#p-search">
      search
     </a>
    </div>
    <div class="mw-content-ltr" dir="ltr" id="mw-content-text" lang="en">
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:352px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:SouthParkHD.png">
        <img alt='four of the main five boys are in the foreground, waving at the viewer. Kenny is climbed on a wooden sign labeled "SOUTH PARK". In the background, the entire population of the city and all the other characters present on the show have gathered, looking at the viewer also.' class="thumbimage" data-file-height="232" data-file-width="430" height="189" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/2/28/SouthParkHD.png/350px-SouthParkHD.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/2/28/SouthParkHD.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/2/28/SouthParkHD.png 2x" width="350"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:SouthParkHD.png" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        <i>
         South Park
        </i>
        title image with the four main characters (
        <a href="/wiki/Eric_Cartman" title="Eric Cartman">
         Eric Cartman
        </a>
        ,
        <a href="/wiki/Stan_Marsh" title="Stan Marsh">
         Stan Marsh
        </a>
        ,
        <a href="/wiki/Kyle_Broflovski" title="Kyle Broflovski">
         Kyle Broflovski
        </a>
        , and
        <a href="/wiki/Kenny_McCormick" title="Kenny McCormick">
         Kenny McCormick
        </a>
        ) in the foreground and most of the recurring, supporting characters in the background
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <p>
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/South_Park" title="South Park">
        South Park
       </a>
      </i>
      is an
      <a href="/wiki/Television_in_the_United_States" title="Television in the United States">
       American
      </a>
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cartoon_series" title="Cartoon series">
       animated television series
      </a>
      created by
      <a href="/wiki/Trey_Parker" title="Trey Parker">
       Trey Parker
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Matt_Stone" title="Matt Stone">
       Matt Stone
      </a>
      for the
      <a href="/wiki/Comedy_Central" title="Comedy Central">
       Comedy Central
      </a>
      <a href="/wiki/Cable_television" title="Cable television">
       lierlevision network
      </a>
      . The ongoing narrative revolves around four children,
      <a href="/wiki/Stan_Marsh" title="Stan Marsh">
       Stan Marsh
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Kyle_Broflovski" title="Kyle Broflovski">
       Kyle Broflovski
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Eric_Cartman" title="Eric Cartman">
       Eric Cartman
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Kenny_McCormick" title="Kenny McCormick">
       Kenny McCormick
      </a>
      , and their bizarre adventures in and around the fictional and eponymous
      <a href="/wiki/Colorado" title="Colorado">
       Colorado
      </a>
      town.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-statesman_1-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-statesman-1">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        1
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      The town is also home to an assortment of characters who make frequent appearances in the show such as
      <a href="/wiki/List_of_students_at_South_Park_Elementary" title="List of students at South Park Elementary">
       students
      </a>
      and their
      <a href="/wiki/List_of_South_Park_families" title="List of South Park families">
       family members
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/List_of_South_Park_Elementary_staff" title="List of South Park Elementary staff">
       elementary school staff
      </a>
      , and
      <a href="/wiki/List_of_recurring_South_Park_characters" title="List of recurring South Park characters">
       recurring characters
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-statesman_1-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-statesman-1">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        1
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      Stan is portrayed as the
      <a href="/wiki/Everyman" title="Everyman">
       everyman
      </a>
      of the group,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-growsup2_2-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-growsup2-2">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        2
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      as the show's official website describes him as "a normal, average, American, mixed-up kid".
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-3">
       <a href="#cite_note-3">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        3
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Kyle is the lone
      <a href="/wiki/Jews" title="Jews">
       Jew
      </a>
      among the group, and his portrayal in this role is often dealt with satirically.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-growsup2_2-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-growsup2-2">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        2
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Stan and Kyle are best friends, and their relationship, which is intended to reflect the real-life friendship between
      <i>
       South Park
      </i>
      creators
      <a href="/wiki/Trey_Parker" title="Trey Parker">
       Trey Parker
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Matt_Stone" title="Matt Stone">
       Matt Stone
      </a>
      ,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-time_4-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-time-4">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        4
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      is a common topic throughout the series. Cartmanloud, obnoxious, and obeseis sometimes portrayed as the series' main antagonist
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NPR_5-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-NPR-5">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        5
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      and whose
      <a href="/wiki/Antisemitism" title="Antisemitism">
       anti-Semitic
      </a>
      attitude has resulted in an ever-progressing rivalry with Kyle.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-growsup2_2-2">
       <a href="#cite_note-growsup2-2">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        2
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Kenny, who comes from a poor family, wears his parka hood so tightly that it covers most of his face and muffles his speech. During the show's first five seasons,
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kenny%27s_deaths" title="Kenny's deaths">
       Kenny would die
      </a>
      in almost every single episode before returning in the next without explanation.
     </p>
     <p>
      Stone and Parker voice most of the male
      <i>
       South Park
      </i>
      characters.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-growsup2_2-3">
       <a href="#cite_note-growsup2-2">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        2
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nytimesmorals_6-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-nytimesmorals-6">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        6
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-faq-23apr2002_7-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-faq-23apr2002-7">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        7
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <a href="/wiki/Mary_Kay_Bergman" title="Mary Kay Bergman">
       Mary Kay Bergman
      </a>
      voiced the majority of the female characters until her death in 1999.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-autogenerated1_8-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-autogenerated1-8">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        8
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <a href="/wiki/Eliza_Schneider" title="Eliza Schneider">
       Eliza Schneider
      </a>
      (19992003),
      <a href="/wiki/Mona_Marshall" title="Mona Marshall">
       Mona Marshall
      </a>
      (2000present), and
      <a href="/wiki/April_Stewart" title="April Stewart">
       April Stewart
      </a>
      (2003present) have voiced most of the female characters since.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-autogenerated1_8-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-autogenerated1-8">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        8
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      A few staff members such as
      <a href="/wiki/Jennifer_Howell" title="Jennifer Howell">
       Jennifer Howell
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Vernon_Chatman" title="Vernon Chatman">
       Vernon Chatman
      </a>
      ,
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/John_Hansen_(voice_actor)" title="John Hansen (voice actor)">
       John Hansen
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Adrien_Beard" title="Adrien Beard">
       Adrien Beard
      </a>
      have voiced the other recurring characters.
     </p>
     <p>
     </p>

     <p>
     </p>
     <h2>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Creation_and_inception">
       Creation and inception
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_South_Park_characters&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Creation and inception">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h2>
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Trey_Parker_Matt_Stone_2007.jpg">
        <img alt="Two seated men. One holds a microphone in one hand and gestures with the other." class="thumbimage" data-file-height="681" data-file-width="1024" height="166" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1a/Trey_Parker_Matt_Stone_2007.jpg/250px-Trey_Parker_Matt_Stone_2007.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1a/Trey_Parker_Matt_Stone_2007.jpg/375px-Trey_Parker_Matt_Stone_2007.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1a/Trey_Parker_Matt_Stone_2007.jpg/500px-Trey_Parker_Matt_Stone_2007.jpg 2x" width="250"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Trey_Parker_Matt_Stone_2007.jpg" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        Matt Stone (right) and Trey Parker (left) created the show and currently voice the majority of the male characters on the show.
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <p>
      Creators
      <a href="/wiki/Trey_Parker" title="Trey Parker">
       Trey Parker
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Matt_Stone" title="Matt Stone">
       Matt Stone
      </a>
      originally conceived the idea of a
      <i>
       South Park
      </i>
      -like show with four children characters, but with a talking stool named Mr. Hankey as the show's main character and planned to call it
      <i>
       The Mr. Hankey Show
      </i>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Commentary_9-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Commentary-9">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        9
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Eventually, Parker and Stone adapted their original idea into a show revolving around the South Park town and four children with Mr. Hankey in a minor supporting role in a future episode.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Commentary_9-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-Commentary-9">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        9
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <a href="/wiki/Comedy_Central" title="Comedy Central">
       Comedy Central
      </a>
      later expressed interest in the series, and picked it up. The premiere episode, "
      <a href="/wiki/Cartman_Gets_an_Anal_Probe" title="Cartman Gets an Anal Probe">
       Cartman Gets an Anal Probe
      </a>
      ", debuted on Comedy Central on August 13, 1997, while Mr. Hankey would debut in the tenth episode, "
      <a href="/wiki/Mr._Hankey,_the_Christmas_Poo" title="Mr. Hankey, the Christmas Poo">
       Mr. Hankey, the Christmas Poo
      </a>
      ".
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HankeyCommentary_10-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-HankeyCommentary-10">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        10
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-DMN0201_11-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-DMN0201-11">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        11
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      In tradition with the show's
      <a href="/wiki/Cutout_animation" title="Cutout animation">
       cutout animation
      </a>
      style, the characters are composed of simple geometrical shapes and uninflected patches of predominantly
      <a href="/wiki/Primary_color" title="Primary color">
       primary colors
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-method_12-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-method-12">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        12
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-avr_13-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-avr-13">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        13
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      They are not offered the same free range of motion associated with hand-drawn characters, as they are mostly shown from only one angle, and their movements are animated in an intentionally jerky fashion.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-growsup2_2-4">
       <a href="#cite_note-growsup2-2">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        2
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-method_12-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-method-12">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        12
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-avr_13-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-avr-13">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        13
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Ever since the show's second episode, "
      <a href="/wiki/Weight_Gain_4000" title="Weight Gain 4000">
       Weight Gain 4000
      </a>
      ", all the characters on the show have been animated with computer software, though they are portrayed to give the impression that the show still utilizes the original technique of cutout animation.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-method_12-2">
       <a href="#cite_note-method-12">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        12
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Cast">
       Cast
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_South_Park_characters&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Cast">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <p>
      Stone and Parker voice most of the male
      <i>
       South Park
      </i>
      characters.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-growsup2_2-5">
       <a href="#cite_note-growsup2-2">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        2
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-faq-23apr2002_7-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-faq-23apr2002-7">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        7
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <a href="/wiki/Mary_Kay_Bergman" title="Mary Kay Bergman">
       Mary Kay Bergman
      </a>
      voiced the majority of the female characters until her death in 1999, near the end of the
      <a href="/wiki/South_Park_(season_3)" title="South Park (season 3)">
       third season
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-autogenerated1_8-2">
       <a href="#cite_note-autogenerated1-8">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        8
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <a href="/wiki/Eliza_Schneider" title="Eliza Schneider">
       Eliza Schneider
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Mona_Marshall" title="Mona Marshall">
       Mona Marshall
      </a>
      succeeded Bergman since 1999, and respectively 2000, with Schneider leaving the show in 2003, after the
      <a href="/wiki/South_Park_(season_7)" title="South Park (season 7)">
       seventh season
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-autogenerated1_8-3">
       <a href="#cite_note-autogenerated1-8">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        8
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      She was replaced by
      <a href="/wiki/April_Stewart" title="April Stewart">
       April Stewart
      </a>
      , who, along with Marshall, continues to voice most of the female characters.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-autogenerated1_8-4">
       <a href="#cite_note-autogenerated1-8">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        8
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Bergman was originally listed in the credits under the alias Shannen Cassidy to protect her reputation as the voice of several
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Disney" title="Disney">
       Disney
      </a>
      characters.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ewbergman_14-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-ewbergman-14">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        14
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Stewart was originally credited under the name Gracie Lazar,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-15">
       <a href="#cite_note-15">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        15
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      while Schneider was sometimes credited under her
      <a href="/wiki/Rock_opera" title="Rock opera">
       rock opera
      </a>
      performance pseudonym Blue Girl.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-16">
       <a href="#cite_note-16">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        16
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      Some
      <i>
       South Park
      </i>
      staff members voice other recurring characters; supervising producer
      <a href="/wiki/Jennifer_Howell" title="Jennifer Howell">
       Jennifer Howell
      </a>
      voices student
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bebe_Stevens" title="Bebe Stevens">
       Bebe Stevens
      </a>
      ,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-faq-23apr2002_7-2">
       <a href="#cite_note-faq-23apr2002-7">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        7
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      writing consultant
      <a href="/wiki/Vernon_Chatman" title="Vernon Chatman">
       Vernon Chatman
      </a>
      voices an
      <a href="/wiki/Anthropomorphism" title="Anthropomorphism">
       anthropomorphic
      </a>
      towel named
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Towlie" title="Towlie">
       Towelie
      </a>
      ,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-faq-23apr2002_7-3">
       <a href="#cite_note-faq-23apr2002-7">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        7
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      and production supervisor
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/John_Hansen_(voice_actor)" title="John Hansen (voice actor)">
       John Hansen
      </a>
      voices
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mr._Slave" title="Mr. Slave">
       Mr. Slave
      </a>
      , the former gay lover of
      <a href="/wiki/Mr._Garrison" title="Mr. Garrison">
       Mr. Garrison
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-faq-21nov2003_17-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-faq-21nov2003-17">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        17
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <i>
       South Park
      </i>
      producer and storyboard artist
      <a href="/wiki/Adrien_Beard" title="Adrien Beard">
       Adrien Beard
      </a>
      , who voices
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Token_Black" title="Token Black">
       Token Black
      </a>
      , the only black kid in
      <i>
       South Park
      </i>
      , was recruited to voice the character "because he was the only black guy [in the] building" when Parker needed to quickly find someone to voice the character during the production of the
      <a href="/wiki/South_Park_(season_4)" title="South Park (season 4)">
       season four
      </a>
      (2000) episode "
      <a href="/wiki/Cartman%27s_Silly_Hate_Crime_2000" title="Cartman's Silly Hate Crime 2000">
       Cartman's Silly Hate Crime 2000
      </a>
      ".
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-faq-30apr2001_18-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-faq-30apr2001-18">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        18
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-hatecrimecomm_19-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-hatecrimecomm-19">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        19
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h2>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Main_characters">
       Main characters
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_South_Park_characters&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Main characters">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h2>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Stan_Marsh">
       Stan Marsh
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_South_Park_characters&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Stan Marsh">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article:
      <a href="/wiki/Stan_Marsh" title="Stan Marsh">
       Stan Marsh
      </a>
     </div>
     <p>
      Stanley Randall "Stan" Marsh is one of the show's four central characters and is voiced by and loosely based on series co-creator Trey Parker.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-time_4-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-time-4">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        4
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-autogenerated2_20-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-autogenerated2-20">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        20
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      He first appeared in
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/The_Spirit_of_Christmas_(short_film)" title="The Spirit of Christmas (short film)">
        The Spirit of Christmas
       </a>
      </i>
      and is portrayed (in words of the show's official website) as "a normal, average, American, mixed-up kid".
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-21">
       <a href="#cite_note-21">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        21
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Stan is a third- then fourth-grade student who commonly has extraordinary experiences not typical of conventional small-town life in his hometown of South Park. In many episodes, Stan contemplates ethics in beliefs, moral dilemmas, and contentious issues, and will often reflect on the lessons he has attained with a speech that often begins with "You know, I learned something today...".
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-philo_22-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-philo-22">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        22
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Kyle_Broflovski">
       Kyle Broflovski
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_South_Park_characters&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Kyle Broflovski">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article:
      <a href="/wiki/Kyle_Broflovski" title="Kyle Broflovski">
       Kyle Broflovski
      </a>
     </div>
     <p>
      Kyle Broflovski is one of the show's four central characters and is voiced by and loosely based on series co-creator
      <a href="/wiki/Matt_Stone" title="Matt Stone">
       Matt Stone
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-faq-23apr2002_7-4">
       <a href="#cite_note-faq-23apr2002-7">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        7
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Having appeared first in
      <i>
       The Spirit of Christmas
      </i>
      shorts, he often displays the highest moral standard of all the boys and is usually depicted as the most intelligent.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-philo2_23-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-philo2-23">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        23
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      When describing Kyle, Stone states that both he and the character are "reactionary", and susceptible to irritability and impatience.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-whois_24-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-whois-24">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        24
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      In some instances, Kyle is the only child in his class to not initially indulge in a fad or fall victim to a ploy. This has resulted in both his eagerness to fit in, and his resentment and frustration.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-philo2_23-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-philo2-23">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        23
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-seriously2_25-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-seriously2-25">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        25
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Kyle is distinctive as one of the few
      <a href="/wiki/Jews" title="Jews">
       Jewish
      </a>
      children on the show, and because of this, he often feels like an outsider amongst the core group of characters.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-whois_24-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-whois-24">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        24
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-wnd_26-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-wnd-26">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        26
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-independent_27-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-independent-27">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        27
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      His portrayal in this role is often dealt with satirically, and has elicited both praise and criticism from Jewish viewers.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nytimesmorals_6-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-nytimesmorals-6">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        6
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-potjdvd_28-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-potjdvd-28">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        28
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mcfarland2_29-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-mcfarland2-29">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        29
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mediatrans_30-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-mediatrans-30">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        30
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Eric_Cartman">
       Eric Cartman
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_South_Park_characters&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Eric Cartman">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article:
      <a href="/wiki/Eric_Cartman" title="Eric Cartman">
       Eric Cartman
      </a>
     </div>
     <p>
      Eric Theodore Cartman first appeared in the 1992 short series "Jesus vs Frosty" and is voiced by Trey Parker.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-faq-23apr2002_7-5">
       <a href="#cite_note-faq-23apr2002-7">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        7
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Cartman has been portrayed as
      <a href="/wiki/Aggression" title="Aggression">
       aggressive
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Prejudice" title="Prejudice">
       prejudiced
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Borderline_personality_disorder" title="Borderline personality disorder">
       emotionally unstable
      </a>
      since his character's inception. These traits are significantly augmented in later seasons as his character evolves, and he begins to exhibit
      <a href="/wiki/Psychopathy" title="Psychopathy">
       psychopathic
      </a>
      and extremely
      <a href="/wiki/Psychological_manipulation" title="Psychological manipulation">
       manipulative
      </a>
      behavior. He is depicted as highly
      <a href="/wiki/Intelligence" title="Intelligence">
       intelligent
      </a>
      , able to execute morally appalling plans and business ideas with success. Among the show's main child characters, Cartman is distinguished as "the fat kid",
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-growsup2_2-6">
       <a href="#cite_note-growsup2-2">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        2
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      for which he is continuously
      <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Weightism&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Weightism (page does not exist)">
       insulted and ridiculed
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-islam_31-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-islam-31">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        31
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Cartman is frequently portrayed as a villain whose actions set in motion the events serving as the main plot of an episode.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NPR_5-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-NPR-5">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        5
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Other children and classmates are alienated by Cartman's insensitive,
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Racist" title="Racist">
       racist
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Homophobia" title="Homophobia">
       homophobic
      </a>
      ,
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Anti-semitism" title="Anti-semitism">
       anti-semitic
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Misogyny" title="Misogyny">
       misogynistic
      </a>
      , lazy, self-righteous, and wildly insecure behavior.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-philo_22-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-philo-22">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        22
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-groce_32-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-groce-32">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        32
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-lowbrow_33-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-lowbrow-33">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        33
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-lear_34-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-lear-34">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        34
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-asullivan_35-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-asullivan-35">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        35
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Cartman often makes anti-semitic insults towards Kyle,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-growsup2_2-7">
       <a href="#cite_note-growsup2-2">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        2
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-AIDS_36-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-AIDS-36">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        36
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      constantly teases Kenny for being poor,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sfrubin_37-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-sfrubin-37">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        37
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      particularly manipulates and mistreats
      <a href="/wiki/Butters_Stotch" title="Butters Stotch">
       Butters Stotch
      </a>
      and displays an extreme disdain for
      <a href="/wiki/Hippie" title="Hippie">
       hippies
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cityjournal_38-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-cityjournal-38">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        38
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-39">
       <a href="#cite_note-39">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        39
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Though he is considered the main antagonist of the series, he has been portrayed as a protagonist or antihero on several occasions.
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Kenny_McCormick">
       Kenny McCormick
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_South_Park_characters&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Kenny McCormick">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article:
      <a href="/wiki/Kenny_McCormick" title="Kenny McCormick">
       Kenny McCormick
      </a>
     </div>
     <p>
      Kenneth "Kenny" McCormick is one of the shows' main characters who debuted in the 1992 short. His oft-muffled and indiscernible speechthe result of his
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Anorak" title="Anorak">
       parka
      </a>
      hood covering his mouthis provided by co-creator Matt Stone.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-faq-23apr2002_7-6">
       <a href="#cite_note-faq-23apr2002-7">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        7
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      He is friends with Stan and Kyle, while maintaining a friendship with Eric Cartman.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nytimessatire_40-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-nytimessatire-40">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        40
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Kenny is regularly teased for living in poverty, particularly by Cartman.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sfrubin_37-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-sfrubin-37">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        37
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Prior to
      <a href="/wiki/South_Park_(season_6)" title="South Park (season 6)">
       season six
      </a>
      , Kenny died in almost every episode, with only a few exceptions.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-41">
       <a href="#cite_note-41">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        note 1
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      The nature of the deaths was often gruesome and portrayed in a comically absurd fashion,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cnnleonard_42-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-cnnleonard-42">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        41
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      and usually followed by Stan and Kyle respectively yelling "Oh my God! They killed Kenny!" and "You bastard(s)!".
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nypost_43-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-nypost-43">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        42
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      In the episode "
      <a href="/wiki/Kenny_Dies" title="Kenny Dies">
       Kenny Dies
      </a>
      ", Kenny dies after developing a
      <a href="/wiki/Terminal_illness" title="Terminal illness">
       terminal
      </a>
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Muscular_disease" title="Muscular disease">
       muscular disease
      </a>
      ,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-buzzle_44-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-buzzle-44">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        43
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      while Parker and Stone claimed that Kenny would not be returning in subsequent episodes and insisted they grew tired of having Kenny die in each episode.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-growsup1_45-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-growsup1-45">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        44
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      For most of season six, his place is taken by
      <a href="/wiki/Butters_Stotch" title="Butters Stotch">
       Butters Stotch
      </a>
      and
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tweek_Tweak" title="Tweek Tweak">
       Tweek Tweak
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-page2_46-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-page2-46">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        45
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ids_47-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-ids-47">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        46
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Nevertheless, Kenny returned from the year-long absence in the season six finale "
      <a href="/wiki/Red_Sleigh_Down" title="Red Sleigh Down">
       Red Sleigh Down
      </a>
      ", and has remained a starring character ever since. His character no longer dies each week, and has only been killed occasionally in episodes following his return.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-48">
       <a href="#cite_note-48">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        47
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Kenny's
      <a href="/wiki/Superhero" title="Superhero">
       superhero
      </a>
      <a href="/wiki/Alter_ego" title="Alter ego">
       alter ego
      </a>
      , Mysterion, first appeared in the season 13 episode "
      <a href="/wiki/The_Coon" title="The Coon">
       The Coon
      </a>
      ".
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-49">
       <a href="#cite_note-49">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        48
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-50">
       <a href="#cite_note-50">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        49
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h2>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Secondary_Characters">
       Secondary Characters
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_South_Park_characters&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Secondary Characters">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h2>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Butters">
       Butters
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_South_Park_characters&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Butters">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article:
      <a href="/wiki/Butters_Stotch" title="Butters Stotch">
       Butters Stotch
      </a>
     </div>
     <p>
      Leopold "Butters" Stotch is cheerful, naive, optimistic, sweet-natured, gullible and more passive relative to the show's other child characters, and can become increasingly anxious, especially when faced with the likelihood of his parents' punishments, which is usually being grounded, usually for no good reason, such as when Butters threatened to "kill" himself as part of a scheme by Stan, Kyle, Kenny and Cartman, and his parents said they would "only" ground him for two weeks if he came down. Butters usually doesn't indulge in foul-mouthed language like the other children and speaks with a mild stutter and tends to fidget with his hands.The other characters perceive him as "nerdy" and he obliviously maintains a very wholesome attitude and mild disposition despite the tragedy and abuse that he frequently encounters from both his classmates and parents. His happy-go-lucky persona has been described as resembling that of a typical 1950s sitcom child character and is usually presented in stark contrast to the harsh treatment he receives at the hands of his friends and strict parents, Butters appeared initially as a background character in first the episode, "Cartman Gets an Anal Probe", but gradually became one of Parker and Stone's favorite characters. Besides wanting to genuinely surprise fans, Parker and Stone killed Kenny at the end of season five to allow an opportunity to provide a major role for Butters, as his following episode, revolves entirely around him. Stan, Kyle, and Cartman allow him into their group as the "fourth friend", but eventually gets ousted and vengefully adopts his super-villain alter ego of Professor Chaos, whom, in spite of his name, only seems to be able to screw things up that either nobody takes notice of, or can be easily resolved. Despite this, Butters has continued to be a major character in recent seasons and continues to be a frequent source of help to Cartman, while also being the main victim of Cartman's constant pranking and manipulation.
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Wendy_Testaburger">
       Wendy Testaburger
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_South_Park_characters&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Wendy Testaburger">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <p>
      <b>
       Wendy Testaburger
      </b>
      is the show's most prominent female student. Her best friend is
      <a href="#Bebe_Stevens">
       Bebe Stevens
      </a>
      , she is the on-and-off girlfriend of
      <a href="#Stan_Marsh">
       Stan
      </a>
      .
      <a href="/wiki/Wendy" title="Wendy">
       Wendy
      </a>
      has previously been voiced by
      <a href="/wiki/Karri_Turner" title="Karri Turner">
       Karri Turner
      </a>
      (in the unaired pilot),
      <a href="/wiki/Mary_Kay_Bergman" title="Mary Kay Bergman">
       Mary Kay Bergman
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Mona_Marshall" title="Mona Marshall">
       Mona Marshall
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Eliza_Schneider" title="Eliza Schneider">
       Eliza Schneider
      </a>
      , and is currently voiced by
      <a href="/wiki/April_Stewart" title="April Stewart">
       April Stewart
      </a>
      . Fellow co-creator
      <a href="/wiki/Matt_Stone" title="Matt Stone">
       Matt Stone
      </a>
      has also cited the name of Wendy Westerberg, the wife of an old friend from his childhood.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-51">
       <a href="#cite_note-51">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        50
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      She wears a pink beret and a purple coat. She has long black hair with uneven bangs. Wendy made her first appearance unnamed, but clearly recognizable, in "
      <a href="/wiki/The_Spirit_of_Christmas_(short_film)" title="The Spirit of Christmas (short film)">
       The Spirit of Christmas
      </a>
      ".
     </p>
     <p>
      Like her boyfriend Stan, Wendy is mature for her age, critical of popular trends, moral and intellectual, as well as being a hardcore
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Feminist" title="Feminist">
       Feminist
      </a>
      , as noted in many of her appearances. She campaigns in several episodes on causes, such as
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Breast_Cancer" title="Breast Cancer">
       Breast Cancer
      </a>
      and the suffering of
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bottlenose_Dolphins" title="Bottlenose Dolphins">
       Bottlenose Dolphins
      </a>
      , often arguing with
      <a href="/wiki/Eric_Cartman" title="Eric Cartman">
       Eric Cartman
      </a>
      who calls her a "bitch" or "ho" in response. Although the two generally only argue, he pushes her to the limit in the
      <a href="/wiki/South_Park_(season_12)" title="South Park (season 12)">
       Season 12 (2008)
      </a>
      episode "
      <a href="/wiki/Breast_Cancer_Show_Ever" title="Breast Cancer Show Ever">
       Breast Cancer Show Ever
      </a>
      " wherein the two engage in a fight on the playground, in which Wendy badly beats up Cartman.
     </p>
     <p>
      Wendy is known to be protective of her relationship with Stan. In the
      <a href="/wiki/South_Park_(season_1)" title="South Park (season 1)">
       Season 1 (1997)
      </a>
      episode "
      <a href="/wiki/Tom%27s_Rhinoplasty" title="Tom's Rhinoplasty">
       Tom's Rhinoplasty
      </a>
      " when Stan, along with the other boys, falls in love with an attractive substitute teacher, with Wendy accusing her of stealing Stan from her, eventually formulating a complex plan to get her thrown into the
      <a href="/wiki/Sun" title="Sun">
       Sun
      </a>
      . She also sometimes displays jealousy  in the
      <a href="/wiki/South_Park_(season_6)" title="South Park (season 6)">
       Season 6 (2002)
      </a>
      episode "
      <a href="/wiki/Bebe%27s_Boobs_Destroy_Society" title="Bebe's Boobs Destroy Society">
       Bebe's Boobs Destroy Society
      </a>
      ", her best friend, Bebe Stevens, receives more attention than she does because of Bebe's developing breasts. Wendy then gets breast implants, but the boys end up ridiculing her after only just realizing the control Bebe's breasts had on them. This behavior is somewhat contradicted by episodes such as "
      <a href="/wiki/Stupid_Spoiled_Whore_Video_Playset" title="Stupid Spoiled Whore Video Playset">
       Stupid Spoiled Whore Video Playset
      </a>
      " and "
      <a href="/wiki/Dances_with_Smurfs" title="Dances with Smurfs">
       Dances with Smurfs
      </a>
      " where she is more concerned with principles than trends and attention.
     </p>
     <p>
      Wendy is very prominent in the show's earlier seasons, usually quarreling with
      <a href="/wiki/Eric_Cartman" title="Eric Cartman">
       Eric Cartman
      </a>
      or reinforcing her relationship with Stan. She speaks in several episodes (especially in the first season) and is often chosen to help the boys out over her classmates. Wendy and Stan's relationship received less focus over the course of the
      <a href="/wiki/South_Park_(season_5)" title="South Park (season 5)">
       Season 5 (2001)
      </a>
      , and she has only one minor role in
      <a href="/wiki/South_Park_(season_6)" title="South Park (season 6)">
       Season 6 (2002)
      </a>
      . This culminates in her breakup with Stan and pairing with Token Black in "
      <a href="/wiki/Raisins_(South_Park)" title="Raisins (South Park)">
       Raisins
      </a>
      ", after which she makes only scattered prominent appearances until the end of the eleventh season, where she gets back together with Stan in "
      <a href="/wiki/The_List_(South_Park)" title="The List (South Park)">
       The List
      </a>
      ". They subsequently pair up as partners on a field trip in "
      <a href="/wiki/Super_Fun_Time" title="Super Fun Time">
       Super Fun Time
      </a>
      ", she beats Cartman in a fight in "
      <a href="/wiki/Breast_Cancer_Show_Ever" title="Breast Cancer Show Ever">
       Breast Cancer Show Ever
      </a>
      " and in the episode "
      <a href="/wiki/Elementary_School_Musical_(South_Park)" title="Elementary School Musical (South Park)">
       Elementary School Musical
      </a>
      " Stan suspects that she may leave him for a popular boy called Bridon. Wendy is able to kiss Stan on the cheek in "
      <a href="/wiki/Elementary_School_Musical_(South_Park)" title="Elementary School Musical (South Park)">
       Elementary School Musical
      </a>
      " without his previous nauseated reaction.
     </p>
     <p>
      Wendy was voted student council president, something first noted in "
      <a href="/wiki/Bebe%27s_Boobs_Destroy_Society" title="Bebe's Boobs Destroy Society">
       Bebe's Boobs Destroy Society
      </a>
      " and re-addressed seven seasons later in "
      <a href="/wiki/Dances_with_Smurfs" title="Dances with Smurfs">
       Dances with Smurfs
      </a>
      ", when Cartman becomes the morning announcer and starts spreading defaming comments about hermost notably her supposed
      <a href="/wiki/Genocide" title="Genocide">
       genocide
      </a>
      of the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Smurfs" title="Smurfs">
       Smurfs
      </a>
      . In response to the allegations, Wendy becomes a guest on Cartman's morning show and manipulates his own story of the Smurf holocaust before announcing her resignation and electing him as the new school council president, effectively relieving him of his morning announcement job. Throughout the episode, Stan solidly defends her.
     </p>

           ]
          </span>
         </a>
        </sup>
       </td>

        A police detective
       </td>

     <h2>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Reception_and_impact">
       Reception and impact
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_South_Park_characters&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Reception and impact">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h2>
     <p>
      Kyle, Eric, Saddam Hussein, Stan and Kenny have all appeared on the cover of
      <i>
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Rolling_Stone_(magazine)" title="Rolling Stone (magazine)">
        Rolling Stone
       </a>
      </i>
      magazine.
     </p>
     <p>
      Cartman is a
      <i>
       South Park
      </i>
      fan favorite,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-islam_31-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-islam-31">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        31
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      and is often described as the most famous character from the series.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NPR_5-2">
       <a href="#cite_note-NPR-5">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        5
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-411mania_68-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-411mania-68">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        67
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-kidsnews_69-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-kidsnews-69">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        68
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      With a headline to their online written version of a radio report,
      <a href="/wiki/NPR" title="NPR">
       NPR
      </a>
      declared Cartman as "America's Favorite Little $@#&amp;*%".
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NPR_5-3">
       <a href="#cite_note-NPR-5">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        5
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      "Respect my authoritah!" and "Screw you guys ...I'm going home!" became catchphrases and, during the show's earlier seasons, were highly popular in the lexicon of viewers.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-perth_70-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-perth-70">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        69
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-oldandnew_71-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-oldandnew-71">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        70
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      His eccentric enunciation of "Hey!" was included in the 2002 edition of
      <i>
       The Oxford Dictionary of Catchphrases
      </i>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-oxford_72-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-oxford-72">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        71
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Stone has said that when fans recognize him or Parker, the fans will usually do their imitation of Cartman, or, in Parker's case, request that he do Cartman's voice.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-page2_46-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-page2-46">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        45
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Both Cartman's commentary and the commentary resulting in response to his actions have been interpreted as statements Parker and Stone are attempting to make to the viewing public,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-seriously_73-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-seriously-73">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        72
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      and these opinions have been subject to much critical analysis in the media and literary world.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bbcnews_74-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-bbcnews-74">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        73
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      Cartman ranked 10th on
      <a href="/wiki/TV_Guide" title="TV Guide">
       TV Guide
      </a>
      's 2002 list of the "Top 50 Greatest Cartoon Characters",
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-TVGuide_75-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-TVGuide-75">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        74
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      24th on
      <a href="/wiki/TV_Guide" title="TV Guide">
       TV Guide
      </a>
      s "25 Greatest TV Villains", 198th on
      <a href="/wiki/VH1" title="VH1">
       VH1
      </a>
      's "200 Greatest Pop Culture Icons",
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-pop_76-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-pop-76">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        75
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      and 19th on
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bravo_(US_TV_channel)" title="Bravo (US TV channel)">
       Bravo
      </a>
      's "100 Greatest TV Characters" television special in 2004.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-77">
       <a href="#cite_note-77">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        76
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      When declaring him the second-scariest character on television (behind only
      <a href="/wiki/Mr._Burns" title="Mr. Burns">
       Mr. Burns
      </a>
      of
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/The_Simpsons" title="The Simpsons">
        The Simpsons
       </a>
      </i>
      ) in 2005,
      <a href="/wiki/MSNBC" title="MSNBC">
       MSNBC
      </a>
      's Brian Bellmont described Cartman as a "bundle of pure, unadulterated evil all wrapped up in a fater, big-bonedcartoony package" who "takes a feral delight in his evildoing".
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-msnbc_78-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-msnbc-78">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        77
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      While Parker and Stone portray Stan and Kyle as having common childlike tendencies, their dialogue is often intended to reflect stances and views on more adult-oriented issues, and have been subject to much critical analysis in the media and literary world and have frequently been cited in publications by experts in the fields of
      <a href="/wiki/Politics" title="Politics">
       politics
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Religion" title="Religion">
       religion
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Popular_culture" title="Popular culture">
       popular culture
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Philosophy" title="Philosophy">
       philosophy
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-usask_79-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-usask-79">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        78
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cnnemmy_80-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-cnnemmy-80">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        79
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nytimesconserv_81-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-nytimesconserv-81">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        80
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-boston_82-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-boston-82">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        81
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-blackwell_83-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-blackwell-83">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        82
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-blmp_84-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-blmp-84">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        83
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-blame_85-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-blame-85">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        84
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Kenny's deaths are well known in popular culture,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nypost_43-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-nypost-43">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        42
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      and was one of the things viewers most commonly associated with
      <i>
       South Park
      </i>
      during its earlier seasons.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-wired_86-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-wired-86">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        85
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      The exclamation of "Oh my God! They killed Kenny!" quickly became a popular
      <a href="/wiki/Catchphrase" title="Catchphrase">
       catchphrase
      </a>
      ,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-time_4-2">
       <a href="#cite_note-time-4">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        4
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-buzzle_44-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-buzzle-44">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        43
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      while both Kenny and the phrase have appeared on some of the more popular pieces of
      <i>
       South Park
      </i>
      merchandise,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nypost_43-2">
       <a href="#cite_note-nypost-43">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        42
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      including shirts, bumper stickers, calendars and baseball caps,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sfrubin_37-2">
       <a href="#cite_note-sfrubin-37">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        37
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      and inspired the rap song "Kenny's Dead" by
      <a href="/wiki/Master_P" title="Master P">
       Master P
      </a>
      ,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nypost_43-3">
       <a href="#cite_note-nypost-43">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        42
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      which was featured on
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Chef_Aid:_The_South_Park_Album" title="Chef Aid: The South Park Album">
        Chef Aid: The South Park Album
       </a>
      </i>
      . The catchphrase also appears in MAD magazine's satire of TITANIC where Stan, Kyle and Cartman are shown on a lifeboat while they were supposedly escaping from the sinking ship. Kenny's deaths have been subject to much critical analysis in the media and literary world.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-green_87-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-green-87">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        86
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-88">
       <a href="#cite_note-88">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        87
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-philo4_89-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-philo4-89">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        88
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      When Sophie Rutschmann of the
      <a href="/wiki/University_of_Strasbourg" title="University of Strasbourg">
       University of Strasbourg
      </a>
      discovered a mutated gene that causes an adult
      <a href="/wiki/Drosophila_melanogaster" title="Drosophila melanogaster">
       fruit fly
      </a>
      to die within two days after it is infected with certain bacteria, she named the gene "Kenny" in honor of the character.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-fruitfly_90-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-fruitfly-90">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        89
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h2>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Merchandise">
       Merchandise
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_South_Park_characters&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Merchandise">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h2>
     <p>
      The characters of
      <i>
       South Park
      </i>
      have spawned several merchandise items, varying from toys to apparel items. In 2004, the first
      <a href="/wiki/Action_figure" title="Action figure">
       action figure
      </a>
      collection was released by Mirage Toys containing five series each with four characters.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-91">
       <a href="#cite_note-91">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        90
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      In 2006,
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mezco" title="Mezco">
       Mezco
      </a>
      toys released a second collection containing a total of six series, each containing six or four figures.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-92">
       <a href="#cite_note-92">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        91
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <a href="/wiki/Comedy_Central" title="Comedy Central">
       Comedy Central
      </a>
      itself has made available a variety of products through its website, including T-shirts, figures, hats, pants, and even shot glasses.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-93">
       <a href="#cite_note-93">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        92
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      A number of fan websites provides an even more extended amount of merchandise, ranging from posters, to magnets, ties and even skateboards, South Park Studios offer through their website the possibility of creating personalized South Park avatars.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-94">
       <a href="#cite_note-94">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        93
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Similar possibilities have been available on multiple fan sites.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-95">
       <a href="#cite_note-95">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        94
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h2>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Notes">
       Notes
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_South_Park_characters&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Notes">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h2>
     <div class="reflist" style="list-style-type: decimal;">
      <ol class="references">
       <li id="cite_note-41">
        <span class="mw-cite-backlink">
         <b>
          <a href="#cite_ref-41">
           ^
          </a>
         </b>
        </span>
        <span class="reference-text">
         Exceptions include "
         <a href="/wiki/Mr._Hankey,_the_Christmas_Poo" title="Mr. Hankey, the Christmas Poo">
          Mr. Hankey, the Christmas Poo
         </a>
         " and "
         <a href="/wiki/Fat_Camp_(South_Park)" title="Fat Camp (South Park)">
          Fat Camp
         </a>
         ". He also seems to die (but turns out to be alive) in some episodes, including "
         <a href="/wiki/Rainforest_Shmainforest" title="Rainforest Shmainforest">
          Rainforest Shmainforest
         </a>
         " and the two-part episode "
         <a href="/wiki/Do_the_Handicapped_Go_to_Hell%3F" title="Do the Handicapped Go to Hell?">
          Do the Handicapped Go to Hell?
         </a>
         " / "
         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Probably_(South_Park_episode)" title="Probably (South Park episode)">
          Probably
         </a>
         ".
        </span>
       </li>
      </ol>
     </div>
